CHAPTER 8
SOLAR ENERGY SYSTEMS
 
SECTION:
4-8-1:   Purpose
4-8-2:   Definitions
4-8-3:   Ground-Mount Solar Systems Prohibited
4-8-4:   Roof-Mount (SES) Permitted As An Accessory Use
4-8-5:   Building Integrated Systems
4-8-6:   Community Solar Gardens (SES) Prohibited
4-8-7:   Commercial/large Scale Solar Farms (SES) Prohibited
4-8-8:   Penalty
4-8-1:   PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to facilitate the construction, installation and
operation of solar energy systems (SES) in the city in a manner that promotes
economic development and ensures the protection of health, safety and welfare,
while also avoiding adverse impacts to important areas such as agricultural
lands, endangered species habitats, conservation lands and other sensitive
lands. It is the intent of this chapter to encourage the development of SES
that reduce reliance on foreign and out- of-state energy resources and bolster
local economic development and job creation. This chapter is not intended to
abridge safety, health or environmental requirements contained in other
applicable codes, standards or ordinances. The provisions of this chapter shall
not be deemed to nullify any provisions of local, state or federal law. (Ord.
24-01, 7-16-2024)
4-8-2:   DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, the following definitions shall apply unless
the context clearly indicates or requires a different meaning.
              As applied to a building, structure or use, one which is on the same lot
ACCESSORY:    with, incidental to and subordinate to the main or principal structure or
              use and which is used for purposes customarily incidental to the main or
              principal structure, or the main or principal use.
BUILDING      A solar energy system that consists of integrating photovoltaic modules
INTEGRATED    into the building structure as the roof or façade and which does not alter
PHOTOVOLTAICS the relief of the roof.
SYSTEMS:
COLLECTIVE    Solar installations owned collectively through subdivision homeowner
SOLAR:        associations, college student groups or other similar arrangements.
COMMERCIAL/   A utility scale commercial facility that converts sunlight to electricity,
LARG E SCALE  whether by photovoltaics, concentrating solar thermal devices or various
SOLAR FARMS:  experimental technologies for onsite or offsite use with the primary
              purpose of selling wholesale or retail generated electricity.
              A community solar-electric (photovoltaic) array, of no more than five acres
COMMUNITY     in size, that provides retail electric power (or financial proxy for retail
SOLAR GARDEN: power) to multiple households or businesses residing in or located off-site
              from the location of the solar energy system.
GROUND-MOUNT  A solar energy system that is directly installed into the ground and is not
SOLAR ENERGY  attached or affixed to an existing structure.
SYSTEM:
              A billing arrangement that allows solar customers to get credit for excess
NET METERING: electricity that they generate and deliver back to the grid so that they
              only pay for their net electricity usage at the end of the month.
PHOTOVOLTAIC  A solar energy system that produces electricity by the use of semiconductor
SYSTEM:       devices calls photovoltaic cells that generate electricity whenever light
              strikes them.
 
                            A trained and qualified electrical professional who
                            has the skills and knowledge related to
QUALIFIED SOLAR INSTALLER:  theconstruction and operation of solar electrical
                            equipment and installations and has received safety
                            training on the hazards involved.
                            A solar energy system in which solar panels are
ROOF-MOUNT:                 mounted on top of a building roof as either a flush
                            mounted system or as modules fixed to frames which
                            can be tilted toward the south at an optical angle.
                            Unobstructed access to direct sunlight on a lot or
                            building through the entire year, including access
SOLAR ACCESS:               across adjacent parcel air rights, for the purpose
                            of capturing direct sunlight to operate a solar
                            energy system.
                            A device, structure or part of a device or
SOLAR COLLECTOR:            structure for which the primary purpose is to
                            transform solar radiant energy into thermal,
                            mechanical, chemical or electrical energy.
                            Radiant energy received from the sun that can be
SOLAR ENERGY:               collected in the form of heat or light by a solar
                            collector.
                            The components and subsystems required to convert
                            solar energy into electric or thermal energy
                            suitable for use. The area of the system includes
SOLAR ENERGY SYSTEM (SES):  all the land inside the perimeter of the system,
                            which extends to any fencing. The term applies, but
                            is not limited to, solar photovoltaic systems,
                            solar thermal systems and solar hot water systems.
                            A component of a solar energy device that is used
SOLAR STORAGE BATTERY/UNIT: to store solar generated electricity or heat for
                            later use.
                            Systems that directly heat water or other liquid
                            using sunlight. The heated liquid is used for such
SOLAR THERMAL SYSTEMS:      purposes as space heating and cooling, domestic hot
                            water and heating pool water.(Ord. 24-01, 7-16-
                            2024)
 
4-8-3:   GROUND-MOUNT SOLAR SYSTEMS PROHIBITED:
Ground-mount solar energy systems are not permitted in the City. (Ord. 24-01,
7-16-2024)
4-8-4:   ROOF-MOUNT (SES) PERMITTED AS AN ACCESSORY USE:
Roof-mount (SES) shall be permitted by a building permit upon application and
accompanying documents in all zoning districts where there is a principal
structure. Before a permit is issued, an application shall be submitted to the
City Zoning Officer demonstrating compliance with this code along with an
affidavit from a Qualified Solar Installer stating said Qualified Solar
Installer has the knowledge and skills related to the construction and
operation of the solar electrical equipment and the date of safety training of
hazards involved.
   (A)   Height. Building or roof-mounted solar energy systems shall not exceed
the maximum allowed height for principal structures in any zoning district.
   (B)   Setbacks. In addition to building setbacks the collector surface and
mounting devises for roof mounted systems shall not extend beyond the exterior
perimeter of the building on which the systems are mounted or built, unless the
collector or mounting system has been engineered to safely extend beyond the
edge, and setback requirements are not violated. Exterior piping for solar hot
water systems shall be allowed to extend beyond the perimeter of the building
on a side yard exposure.
   (C)   Reflection angles. Reflection angles for solar collectors shall be
oriented such that they do not project glare onto adjacent properties. All
installations shall be manufactured with anti-glare technology.
   (D)   Safety.
      (1)   Roof-mounted or building-mounted solar energy systems, excluding
building integrated systems, shall allow for adequate roof access for
firefighting purposes.
      (2)   Roof-mounted or building-mounted solar energy systems shall meet
the requirements of this code of ordinances.
      (3)   All solar energy systems shall be installed by a qualified solar
installer and plans sealed by, or a letter signed by, a structural engineer or
architect indicating the weight of the solar installation does not exceed the
allowable loading for the roof structure according to the applicable building
code.
      (4)   Any connection to the public utility grid shall be inspected by the
appropriate public utility.
      (5)   The installation shall be designed such that the amount of
electricity generated does not exceed 125% of the typical amount consumed for
the needs of the household.
      (6)   All solar energy systems shall be maintained and kept in good
working order. If it is determined by the city’s Code Compliance Officer that a
solar energy system is not being maintained, kept in good working order or is
no longer being utilized to perform as intended for six consecutive months, the
property owner shall be given 30- day notice for removal of the unit and all
equipment. If the solar energy system is not removed within 30 days, the Code
Compliance Officer shall issue a notice of violation.
      (7)   Upon the operation of the solar energy system, the homeowner shall
allow reasonable access to the solar energy system by the city and its agents
for the purpose of fire hazard training and other inspections.
   (E)   Approved solar components. Electric solar energy system components
shall have a UL listing or approved equivalent and solar hot water systems
shall have an SRCC rating.
   (F)   Restrictions on solar energy systems limited. Consistent with 765 ILCS
165, no homeowner’s agreement, covenant, common interest community or other
contracts between multiple property owners within the city shall prohibit or
restrict homeowners from installing solar energy systems. (Ord. 24-01, 7-16-
2024)
4-8-5:   BUILDING INTEGRATED SYSTEMS:
Building integrated systems shall be permitted outright in all zoning
districts, but shall meet the requirements of the city’s zoning and building
code. (Ord. 24-01, 7-16-2024)
4-8-6: COMMUNITY SOLAR GARDENS (SES) PROHIBITED:
Community solar gardens (SES) are not permitted in the city. (Ord. 24-01, 7-16-
2024)
4-8-7: COMMERCIAL/LARGE SCALE SOLAR FARMS (SES) PROHIBITED:
Commercial/large scale solar farm (SES) are not permitted in the city. (Ord.
24-01, 7-16-2024)
4-8-8: PENALTY:
Anyone convicted of violation any section of this Code shall be fined in the
sum of not less than $250.00, nor more than $750.00. (Ord. 24-01, 7-16-2024)
TITLE 5
FIRE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
FIRE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
5-1-1: Department Established
5-1-2: Mayor To Supervise
5-1-3: Officers
5-1-4: Salaries
5-1-5: Rules, Bylaws
5-1-6: Duty Of Department
5-1-7: Equipment
5-1-8: Maintenance Of Equipment
5-1-9: Interfere, Resist Officers
5-1-10: Unlawful Use Of Apparatus
5-1-11: Injury To Apparatus
5-1-12: Illinois Fire Protection Training Act; Participation Required
5-1-1: DEPARTMENT ESTABLISHED:
The Atlanta volunteer fire department shall consist of the mayor, the aldermen,
the chief of police, the street commissioner, the superintendent of water and
all police officers of the city, and such other persons as may be members.
(Ord. 6, 2-6-1917)
5-1-2: MAYOR TO SUPERVISE:
The mayor shall have and exercise a general supervision over the fire
department and he shall report to the city council quarterly at their first
regular meetings in April, July, October and January of each year, and more
often if necessary, the condition of the engines, hose, hooks and ladders,
buckets and other fire apparatus belonging to the fire department, and also the
condition of the buildings in which they are kept and shall recommend such
additions or improvements as he may deem necessary and expedient. (Ord. 6, 2-6-
1917)
5-1-3: OFFICERS:
The officers of the volunteer fire department shall consist of a fire chief, an
assistant fire chief, three (3) captains and a secretary-treasurer. The fire
chief shall be appointed to serve for a one year period and shall be appointed
by the mayor, by and with the consent of the city council. The assistant fire
chief shall be appointed by the fire chief for a one year term which shall
coincide with the tenure of the fire chief. The three (3) captains and the
secretary- treasurer shall be elected by the members of the department for a
one year term, such election to take place at the annual meeting of the Atlanta
volunteer fire department to be held in January of each year. (Ord. 78-11, 5-
16-1978)
5-1-4: SALARIES:
The salaries of the officers and members of the volunteer fire department, both
by the year and for attendance at fires, and the manner of the payment of such
salaries, shall be determined by the department, subject to the approval of the
city council, at the annual meeting of the volunteer fire department to be held
in January of each year. (Ord. 78-3, 1-12-1978)
5-1-5: RULES, BYLAWS:
The members of the volunteer fire department shall adopt such bylaws concerning
meetings (which shall be required monthly), membership, etc., as are consistent
with the provisions of this chapter. (1972 Code)
5-1-6: DUTY OF DEPARTMENT:
It shall be the duty of the fire department to lead in and to direct the
gaining control of and extinguishing of fires in the city, and in preserving
and protecting property from loss by fire, water and theft. (Ord. 6, 2-6-1917)
5-1-7: EQUIPMENT:
The city council shall from time to time procure the necessary engines, hose,
hooks and ladders, buckets and other fire apparatus for the use of the fire
department, and shall provide convenient places for the safekeeping thereof.
(Ord. 6, 2-6-1917)
5-1-8: MAINTENANCE OF EQUIPMENT:
It shall be the duty of the fire chief to keep all fire apparatus in the best
of order and ready for immediate use; and whenever any such apparatus needs
repairing, he shall immediately notify the mayor, who shall without delay cause
all necessary repairs to be made. (Ord. 6, 2-6-1917)
5-1-9: INTERFERE, RESIST OFFICERS:
Whoever shall at any fire wilfully hinder, delay, resist or obstruct any
officer, firefighter or other person in the discharge of his duty, or shall
neglect or refuse to obey or observe the lawful command of any officer, or
shall conduct himself in a riotous or disorderly manner at any fire, shall in
each case be subject to the penalty provided by section
1-4-1 of this code, and for incapacity, neglect of duty or misconduct of any
firefighter, the city council may remove him from the fire department. (Ord. 6,
2-6-1917)
5-1-10: UNLAWFUL USE OF APPARATUS:
No person shall use any fire apparatus for any private purpose, nor, without
authority, remove the same from the proper place of deposit thereof, without
consent of the city council. No person having charge of any fire apparatus
shall permit the same to be used for private purposes, and any person so
violating this provision shall be subject to the penalty provided by section
1-4-1 of this code and shall be liable for any damage to said apparatus that
may occur. (Ord. 6, 2-6-1917)
5-1-11: INJURY TO APPARATUS:
Whoever shall wilfully, maliciously or negligently break, deface or destroy or
otherwise injure any fire apparatus belonging to the city or any fire company,
shall be subject to the penalty provided by section
1-4-1 of this code and, in addition thereto, the expenses which may be incurred
in repairing the injuries committed shall be added to the penalty and form a
part thereof. (Ord. 6, 2-6-1917)
5-1-12: ILLINOIS FIRE PROTECTION TRAINING ACT; PARTICIPATION REQUIRED:
   (A)   Participation: The city hereby elects to participate in the programs
provided for in the Illinois fire protection training act.
   (B)   Certification Required: Before an individual may commence regular full
time employment as a firefighter, he must have been certified by the Illinois
state fire marshal as a firefighter II, as having successfully completed an
approved training course as provided in said act.
   (C)   Completion Time Limit: The firefighter II training must be completed
by the trainee within his probationary period of six (6) months, except for
volunteers, part time and paid on call personnel. (Ord. 82-5, 9-21-1982)
CHAPTER 2
FIRE PREVENTION CODE
SECTION:
5-2-1: Adoption Of Fire Prevention Code
5-2-2: Additions, Insertions And Changes
5-2-3: Key Boxes Required For Buildings
5-2-1: ADOPTION OF FIRE PREVENTION CODE:
A certain document, three (3) copies of which are on file in the office of the
city clerk, being marked and designated as the BOCA national fire prevention
code, 1996 edition, as published by the Building Officials and Code
Administrators International, Inc., be and is hereby adopted as the fire
prevention code of the city for the control of buildings and structures as
herein provided; and each and all of the regulations, provisions, penalties,
conditions and terms of said BOCA national fire prevention code, are hereby
referred to, adopted and made a part hereof as if fully set out in this
chapter, with the additions, insertions, deletions and changes, if any,
prescribed in section
5-2-2 of this chapter. (Ord. 99-01, 3-2-1999)
5-2-2: ADDITIONS, INSERTIONS AND CHANGES:
The BOCA national fire prevention code, 1996 edition, is amended and changed to
read in the following respects:
Section 100.1: Title: These regulations as set forth herein shall be known as
the fire prevention code of the city of Atlanta and are herein referred to as
such or as "this code".
(Ord. 99-01, 3-2-1999)
5-2-3: KEY BOXES REQUIRED FOR BUILDINGS:
   (A)   Buildings, General: All new commercial and/or manufacturing buildings
constructed after the effective date hereof, and all existing commercial and/or
manufacturing buildings shall be required to comply within twelve (12) months
of the effective date hereof. Any commercial and/or manufacturing buildings
requesting the city fire department to either retain or obtain access to the
building shall be required to use a master key Knox box at a location approved
by the fire department. Such box shall be provided with master keys necessary
for access to all portions of the premises. Such box and keys shall be provided
any time the building shall change. This section does not apply to residential
dwellings under four (4) units.
   (B)   Buildings With Elevators: Any buildings equipped with elevators who
desire to make accessible to the Knox box system shall provide:
      1.   Two (2) sets of keys for entry to building and all portions of
premises.
      2.   Two (2) sets of elevator control keys if elevators are equipped with
fire department bypass switches. (Ord. 99-01, 3-2-1999)
CHAPTER 3
FIREWORKS
SECTION:
5-3-1: Fireworks; Permit
5-3-2: Explosives
5-3-3: Rules Of State Fire Marshal
5-3-1: FIREWORKS; PERMIT:
   (A)   Discharge: It shall be unlawful to discharge or set off any fireworks,
or give or exhibit any pyrotechnic displays in the city excepting that public
displays which are licensed may be given at any time permitted by the license.
   (B)   Displays: No public exhibition of fireworks or pyrotechnics shall be
given unless a permit therefor is first secured from the mayor. All such public
displays shall be under the supervision of a competent person, and shall be
superintended by the chief of police or some member of the police department
assigned to this duty by him.
   (C)   Sales: No person shall sell or offer for sale or keep for the purpose
of so doing, any fireworks in the city. (1972 Code)
5-3-2: EXPLOSIVES:
It shall be unlawful to keep or store any nitroglycerine or other explosive
commonly known as TNT in the city in any quantities, excepting for medicinal
purposes or laboratory purposes and for such purposes no more than one pound
shall be stored in any one building or premises. (1972 Code)
5-3-3: RULES OF STATE FIRE MARSHAL:
All explosives must be kept or stored in accordance with the rules enforced by
the state fire marshal with regard to the same, subject to the conditions of
this chapter. (1972 Code)
CHAPTER 4
PROHIBITED BURNING
SECTION:
5-4-1: Burning Prohibited
5-4-1: BURNING PROHIBITED:
   (A)   Prohibitions: No person shall cause, allow, aid, suffer or maintain
any open burning of any kind, or the burning of any waste materials or rubbish
in any incinerator, barrel, can, pit, fireplace or similar container or
enclosure. No person in charge or possession of any premises upon which such
burning occurs, or any premises immediately adjacent to any public place upon
which such burning occurs, shall fail to extinguish the fire, providing he has
knowledge of the fire and it is within his power to extinguish it.
   (B)   Exceptions: This section shall not apply to the following:
      1.   An indoor or outdoor barbecue or similar heating or cooking device
while being used for the heating or cooking of food for human consumption and
not being used primarily for the burning of waste materials or rubbish.
      2.   A pathological type incinerator or furnace used by a hospital,
veterinary hospital, crematorium or similar establishment for the incineration
of body parts, bandages or related refuse.
      3.   Comfort heating by use of a fireplace inside of a residence that is
not being used primarily for the burning of waste materials or rubbish.
      4.   The personal use of cigarettes, cigars or pipes.
      5.   The using of matches for the lighting of authorized fire or fire fed
devices.
      6.   The use of authorized lighting and heating devices such as candles,
water heaters and lanterns, provided they are not likely to cause air pollution
or create fire hazards.
      7.   Controlled fires for the purpose of training firefighters. (1972
Code)
      8.   Burning of landscape waste upon the premises where it is produced.
For purposes of this subsection, "landscape waste" shall be defined as leaves,
grass and shrubbery trimmings, twigs and tree branches; provided, however, that
no landscape waste shall be burned within the city limits after the hour of
seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. (Ord. 82-6, 10-5-1982)
TITLE 6
POLICE REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
POLICE DEPARTMENT
SECTION:
6-1-1: Department Established
6-1-2: Mayor Head Of Department
6-1-3: Chief Of Police; General Powers And Duties
6-1-4: Department Powers And Duties
6-1-5: Police Officers Commissioned; Compensation
6-1-6: Part Time Police Chief And Part Time Police Officers
6-1-1: DEPARTMENT ESTABLISHED:
There is hereby established a police department of the city, which shall
consist of the mayor, aldermen, chief of police and such police officers as may
from time to time be appointed by the mayor and approved by the city council.
The position of the chief of police is established as an officer of the city as
defined in title 1, chapter 5 of this code and the chief of police is subject
to all provisions in title 1, chapter 5 of this code. (Ord. 96-05, 6-18-1996)
6-1-2: MAYOR HEAD OF DEPARTMENT:
   (A)   Duties: The mayor shall be the head of the police department and shall
superintend and direct the police generally. He shall see that the several
members of the department are prompt and faithful in the discharge of their
duties and shall, from time to time, take such measures for the preservation of
the peace and good order of the city as he may deem necessary, and shall see
that all ordinances thereof are duly observed and enforced. (Ord. 5, 2-6-1917)
   (B)   Appointment Of Officers: The mayor is hereby authorized to appoint, by
and with the advice and consent of the city council, such persons of a suitable
character, special police officers, whenever in his judgment he shall deem it
to be necessary. The term of office of any such special police officer shall
not exceed that of the mayor. If any such appointment is made prior to the
advice and consent of the city council having been first obtained, such
appointment shall come before the city council for its advice and consent no
later than the next regularly scheduled meeting of the city council. Special
police officers shall have all the powers heretofore granted to members of the
police department. (Ord. 82-7, 11-2-1982)
6-1-3: CHIEF OF POLICE; GENERAL POWERS AND DUTIES:
   (A)   Enforcement: It shall be the duty of the chief of police to enforce
all penal ordinances as hereinafter provided, keep order and prevent
disturbances or violations of all provisions of this code; to serve all
subpoenas, summons, warrants, executions and all other writs or notices for and
on behalf of the city, promptly and efficiently, and to perform all other
duties or acts that may be required of him by this or any other provision of
this code, either in express terms or such as may be clearly implied, and to
obey all instructions of the city council or the mayor pertaining to his
official duties.
   (B)   Complaints: It shall be the duty of the chief of police or any police
officer of the city, while on duty, on hearing or being informed of the
violation of any provisions of this code, to immediately obtain all the
information relating thereto, and inform the city attorney thereof, and if
requested by the city attorney to do so, shall make complaint of such violation
under oath before the proper officer of the city.
   (C)   Arrest: It shall be the duty of the chief of police and any police
officer on duty, to immediately arrest any and all persons violating any penal
ordinance of the city, in the presence or view of such officer, with or without
a warrant, and forthwith take such offender before the proper officer in the
city and make a complaint under oath against such person or persons, setting
forth the offense committed, and notify the city attorney of such arrest, and
attend before such proper officer to prosecute such persons according to law.
   (D)   Develop Policies: It shall be the duty and responsibility of the chief
of police to develop policies for the police department and to implement said
policies within the police department. The chief of police will administer the
internal workings and day to day business of the police department. The chief
of police will have the authority to make public statements on any matters
which affect the public as they apply to potential dangers, prevalent crime or
traffic conditions, police/community relations, proposed legislation, or other
issues affecting or related to public safety, policing, or the police
department in general.
   (E)   Neglect Of Duties: If the chief of police or any police officer
refuses or neglects to perform any duty required of him by this or any other
provision of this code now in force, or such as may hereafter be passed, he
shall be subject to a penalty.
   (F)   Compensation: The chief of police and police officers shall receive
such compensation as the city council may from time to time determine. (Ord.
96-05, 6-18-1996)
6-1-4: DEPARTMENT POWERS AND DUTIES:
   (A)   Arrest Authority: All members of the police department shall have
power to arrest or cause to be arrested, with or without process, all persons
who shall break the peace or be found violating any provision of this code, and
shall have power to detain or order the detention of all such persons in
custody in some safe place overnight, until such persons can be duly examined
by and before some competent court or proper officer.
   (B)   Enforcement: It shall be the duty of the members of the police
department to enforce all provisions of this code, and to preserve peace and
good order in the city. (Ord. 5, 2-6-1917)
6-1-5: POLICE OFFICERS COMMISSIONED; COMPENSATION:
   (A)   Commissioned: Police officers appointed by the mayor and approved by
the city council shall, before they enter upon the discharge of their duties,
be commissioned under the corporate seal, signed by the mayor or presiding
officer of the city council and city clerk, and shall receive such pay for
their services as the city council shall from time to time allow.
   (B)   Compensation: The chief of police and police officers shall be
entitled in addition to their salary or per diem the same fees that are now or
may hereafter be allowed by the laws of this state to constables for like
services in making arrests, serving summonses, etc., to be collected as costs
from the offenders or property sold, except where the fees are fixed by
ordinance and a different mode provided for its collection or payment. (Ord. 5,
2-6-1917)
6-1-6: PART TIME POLICE CHIEF AND PART TIME POLICE OFFICERS:
   (A)   Qualifications: In accordance with Illinois state law, 65 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 5/3.1-30-21, the city of Atlanta establishes the following
hiring standards for part time police officers:
      1.   Be a citizen of the United States; and
      2.   Be twenty one (21) years of age; and
      3.   Be a high school graduate or the equivalent; and
      4.   Possess a valid Illinois driver's license; and
      5.   Possess a current Illinois firearms owner identification card; and
      6.   Have no felony criminal record; and if a misdemeanor criminal
record, a copy of the record should be submitted with the written application
required in subsection (A)12 of this section and an explanation if required by
the chief of police to explain all circumstances of the record; and
      7.   Submit fingerprints for examination by Illinois state police bureau
of identification and federal bureau of investigation; and
      8.   Submit to a physical examination, at the expense of the city of
Atlanta, and be found drug free and in good general health; and
      9.   Pass a written exam if the city council opts to administer a
standard entry level law enforcement test; and
      10.   Submit to an oral interview before the city council or its police
committee; and
      11.   Be trained in accordance with the Illinois police training act, as
may be amended from time to time, and the rules and requirements of the
Illinois law enforcement training and standards board; and
      12.   Submit a written application and/or resume to the chief of police
or the mayor in the case of a part time police chief appointment.
   (B)   Appointment: The mayor is hereby authorized to appoint, by and with
the advice and consent of the city council, such persons of a suitable
character, a part time police chief or part time police officers, whenever in
his judgment he shall deem it to be necessary, but the number of hours a part
time officer may work within a calendar year is restricted.
   (C)   Compensation: The part time police chief and part time police officers
shall receive such compensation as the city council may from time to time
determine. (Ord. 12-05, 5-1-2012)
