ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL; DOGS AND CATS
6-3-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
For the purposes of this chapter:
ANIMAL: Any and all types of animals, both domesticated and wild, male and
female, singular and plural.
AT LARGE: Any animal found upon the public streets, sidewalks, alleys, parkways
or any unenclosed place, unless such animal is firmly held on a leash or is in
an enclosed vehicle.
BITING: To seize or pierce the clothing or skin, or attempt to seize or pierce
the clothing or skin, of a person or the skin of another animal, by the teeth
of an animal.
CRUELTY TO ANIMALS: Includes, but is not necessarily limited to, the following:
   (A)   Overloading, overdriving, overworking, beating, torturing, abusing,
tormenting, knowingly poisoning, knowingly attempting to poison, mutilating or
killing any animal or causing or knowingly permitting the same to be done.
   (B)   Working any old, lame, infirm, sick or disabled animal, or causing or
knowingly permitting the same to be done.
   (C)   Unnecessarily failing to provide an animal in one's charge or custody,
as owner or otherwise, with proper food, drink and proper sanitary shelter.
   (D)   Abandoning any old, lame, infirm, sick or disabled animal by leaving
such animal on any highway or public way or in any other place where it may
suffer injury, hunger, exposure or become a public charge.
DANGEROUS DOG: Any dog which has bitten any person or which causes reasonable
fear of bodily injury to any person by attacking or threatening to attack such
person.
DOG: Any and all animals of the canine species.
KENNEL: Any premises or portions thereof on which four (4) or more dogs, cats
or other household domestic animals, or any combination thereof, over four (4)
months of age are kept.
OWNER: (A) Any person owning, harboring or keeping an animal within the city.
   (B)   For purposes of this chapter, the person last issued a dog license
shall be presumed to be the owner of such dog.
   (C)   A person harboring or keeping an unlicensed animal in the city for a
period of five (5) days shall be presumed to be the owner of such animal. (1972
Code; amd. Ord. 80-101, 2-19-1980, eff. 3-11-1980; Ord. 06-04, 3-21-2006; Ord.
06-08, 7-25-2006)
6-3-1-2: DOG LICENSE REQUIRED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to own, possess or maintain any dog within
the city without first securing any license or tag required by state or county
law, or by this code. (1972 Code)
6-3-1-3: EXCEPTIONS:
(Rep. by Ord. 80-101, 2-19-1980, eff. 3-11-1980)
6-3-1-4: UNAUTHORIZED TRANSFER OF LICENSE:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place any license tag on any dog other
than the dog for which such tag was issued. (1972 Code)
6-3-1-5: TAG TO BE AFFIXED TO COLLAR:
   (A)   Requirements: The owner of a dog shall provide the dog with a collar
or harness made of leather, metal or other substantial material, to which shall
be securely fastened all proper license tags and also a tag issued by the state
rabies inspector, deputy inspector or any licensed veterinarian showing that
such dog has been vaccinated against rabies during the current or immediately
preceding year.
   (B)   Impound For Violation: A dog found within the city not wearing the
proper collar and tags shall be impounded. (1972 Code; amd. Ord. 1001, 5-16-
1972)
6-3-1-6: UNAUTHORIZED REMOVAL OF COLLAR OR TAGS:
It shall be unlawful for any person not authorized by the owner to remove or
take away any dog or cat collar or rabies vaccination tag from any dog or cat;
provided, however, that this section shall not apply to any governmental
official in the exercise of his duties. (Ord. 91-10, 11-5-1991)
6-3-1-7: PENALTIES:
In addition to the other penalties provided by this chapter, the following
penalty shall be assessed against the owner for the following violations:
   (A)   Allowing a dog to run at large in violation of section
6-3-3-5 of this chapter, or allowing a cat to violate the terms and provisions
hereof:
 
First offense        $ 35.00
Second offense       60.00
Subsequent offenses  110.00
 
   (B)   Allowing a dangerous dog to run at large in violation of section
6-3-3-13 of this chapter:
 
First offense                   $ 35.00
Second and subsequent offenses  110.00
 
   (C)   In addition to the penalties listed in subsections (A) and (B) of this
section, the owner shall pay to the city a boarding fee of twenty five dollars
($25.00) per day for each day the city temporarily impounds the owner's animal
for a violation of any provision of this chapter. (Ord. 06-08, 7-25-2006)
6-3-1-8: COLLAR REQUIRED; CATS:
No person shall own, possess, keep, maintain or harbor any cat over four (4)
months of age without providing such cat with a collar to be worn at all times.
Collars shall be a humane breakaway type or suitable harness. (Ord. 91-10, 11-
5-1991)
6-3-1-9: IDENTIFICATION TAGS REQUIRED; CATS:
All cats shall have affixed to their collars or harness an identification tag
stating the owner's name, current address and telephone number. (Ord. 91-10,
11-5-1991)
6-3-1-10: IMPOUNDMENT OF CATS CREATING NUISANCES:
No person owning, possessing or harboring any cat shall permit his/her animal
to become a nuisance. A cat shall be considered a nuisance if said animal:
   (A)   Substantially damages property other than that of the owner; or
   (B)   Causes unsanitary, dangerous or unreasonably offensive conditions; or
   (C)   Causes a disturbance by excessive caterwauling or other noisemaking;
or
   (D)   Interferes with any person or domestic animals while off the premises
of the cat owner.
Any cat found to be violating any of the provisions hereof shall be taken up
and impounded whenever possible, and any city officer or the duly designated
representatives of the city officers or officials shall be hereby authorized to
impound such cats. (Ord. 91-10, 11-5-1991)
ARTICLE II. RABIES CONTROL
6-3-2-1: RABIES VACCINATION REQUIRED:
The owner of a dog four (4) months or more of age, located within the city,
shall cause such dog to be inoculated by the state rabies inspector, or by his
deputy or by any licensed veterinarian. (1972 Code)
6-3-2-2: CERTIFICATE OF VACCINATION:
Every licensed veterinarian who vaccinates a dog shall issue a certificate of
vaccination to the owner of such dog stating the name and address of the owner,
a brief description of the dog and the date of such vaccination. (1972 Code)
6-3-2-3: DUTIES OF OWNER:
   (A)   Any owner receiving notice or having knowledge that his dog has been
bitten by any animal suffering or suspected to be suffering from rabies, or
that his dog has bitten any person, shall immediately notify or deliver his dog
to any police officer, who shall place the dog in a licensed veterinary
hospital for observation, or such owner shall himself immediately notify the
city clerk of the name and location of such hospital.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any owner of a dog, upon receiving notice or
having knowledge that such dog has bitten any person or that such dog has been
bitten by any animal suffering or suspected to be suffering from rabies, to
sell or give away such dog, or permit such dog to run at large, or to be taken
beyond the city, except to a veterinary hospital within the county; and it
shall also be unlawful for such owner to refuse to deliver said dog for
observation as provided herein. (1972 Code)
6-3-2-4: DUTIES OF PERSONS SUSPECTING ANY DOG TO BE SUFFERING FROM RABIES:
   (A)   Reporting Required: Every veterinarian or other person discovering or
suspecting any dog to be suffering from rabies shall immediately report this
matter to the police department, giving the name and address of the owner of
such dog, if known, the place where the dog can be found and the license tag
number of such dog, if known.
   (B)   Presumption Of Rabies: For the purposes of this section only, any dog
which has bitten any person shall be presumed to be suffering from rabies.
(1972 Code)
6-3-2-5: DUTIES OF POLICE DEPARTMENT:
Upon being notified that a dog has bitten any person or is suspected of
suffering from rabies, the police department shall:
   (A)   When the owner of the dog is known, notify such owner and direct such
owner to deliver up the dog to a licensed veterinary hospital for observation;
or
   (B)   When the owner of the dog is unknown, immediately take up said dog and
confine said dog to a licensed veterinary hospital for observation.
   (C)   When a dog is taken up under the provisions of subsection (B) of this
section, notify the owner, if known, of the confinement of such dog within
seven (7) days after the confinement begins or the identity of the owner is
discovered. (1972 Code)
6-3-2-6: CONFINEMENT FOR OBSERVATION:
   (A)   Required: Confinement of a dog for observation under this article
shall be for a period of ten (10) days. The dog shall be examined immediately
after confinement and again before the ten (10) day period has expired.
   (B)   Veterinarian Certificate: The veterinarian shall submit to the city
clerk a certificate following each examination stating whether or not the dog
shows symptoms of rabies.
   (C)   Determination Of Rabies: If the dog is found to be rabid, the dog
shall be destroyed in a humane manner. If the dog is destroyed, or if it shall
die within the ten (10) day observation period, its head shall be sent by the
veterinarian to the laboratory of the state department of public health.
   (D)   Release: If the dog is not found rabid by the end of the confinement
period, the owner shall be so notified and the dog may be released to its
owner, and the city clerk so advised. (1972 Code)
6-3-2-7: RABIES EPIDEMIC; POWER OF MAYOR:
   (A)   Proclamation: Whenever the mayor shall deem it necessary to prevent an
epidemic of rabies, he may issue a proclamation requiring the owners of all
dogs to keep them securely confined or to keep them properly muzzled or
leashed, so they cannot bite, for such times as may be designated in the
proclamation or until otherwise notified.
   (B)   Publication: The mayor shall publish such proclamation in a paper of
general circulation within the city and post such proclamation in the city
hall. (1972 Code)
6-3-2-8: DUTIES OF OWNERS UPON PROCLAMATION OF RABIES EPIDEMIC:
Following any proclamation as set forth in section
6-3-2-7 of this article, it shall be unlawful for any owner to permit his dog
to run at large in violation of the provisions of such proclamation. In
addition to the penalties provided with respect to any such owner for violating
this section, a dog running at large unmuzzled shall be impounded. (1972 Code)
6-3-2-9: POLICE AUTHORIZED TO KILL CERTAIN DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE:
Any police officer may kill a dog running at large which is suspected of
suffering from rabies if the dog, in the opinion of the police officer, cannot
be safely taken up and impounded, or if the police officer deems such killing
essential to the safety of any person. (1972 Code)
6-3-2-10: FALSE REPORTS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to make any report required by this article
without having a reasonable belief in its truth and accuracy. (1972 Code)
ARTICLE III. OFFENSES INVOLVING ANIMALS
6-3-3-1: ANNOYING NOISES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to keep or harbor any animal which disturbs
the peace by loud noises at any time of day or night, and it shall be unlawful
for any such person to permit any animal to make such noises. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-2: CAUSING ANIMAL TO MAKE ANNOYING NOISES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to treat any animal in any manner which
causes such animal to disturb the peace by loud noises at any time of day or
night. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-3: COMPLAINT OF ANNOYING NOISES:
Any person residing in a neighborhood whose quietness has been disturbed by any
animal owned or possessed within the neighborhood may make a sworn complaint
before a police officer or the city clerk against the owner or possessor of
said animal. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-4: ANIMALS DISTURBING THE PEACE DECLARED NUISANCE:
Any animal which disturbs the peace by loud noises at any time of day or night
is hereby declared to be a nuisance, and may be impounded by a police officer.
(1972 Code)
6-3-3-5: DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE:
It shall be unlawful for any person owning or possessing any dog within the
city to permit such dog to run at large. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-6: DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE DECLARED NUISANCE:
Any dog running at large is hereby declared to be a nuisance, and may be taken
up and impounded by any police officer. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-7: DEFECATION BY DOGS ON PRIVATE PROPERTY:
It shall be unlawful for any owner or possessor to permit a dog to walk or
defecate upon private property without the consent of the occupant thereof.
(1972 Code)
6-3-3-8: DESTRUCTION OF PRIVATE PROPERTY BY DOG:
It shall be unlawful for any owner or possessor of any dog to permit such dog
to damage or destroy any personal property of another person. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-9: RESTRICTION OF ANIMALS FROM PUBLIC PLACES:
It shall be unlawful for any owner or possessor of any animal to permit such
animal to enter any religious premises, public hall, bank building, automobile
gasoline station, public garage or any place where food or beverage is sold or
served during such time as those establishments are open for use to the public
or persons entitled to use the same; provided, however, that the owner of any
of the above establishments may permit a watch dog to remain therein if such
dog is held and restrained in such a way that such dog cannot injure any patron
or come in contact with any food. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-10: THREATENING OR ANNOYING DOGS:
It shall be unlawful for any owner or possessor of any dog to permit such dog
to cause reasonable fear of bodily injury to any person by attacking or
threatening to attack such person, or to permit such dog to jump upon any
person to the annoyance of said person. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-11: DOGS CHASING VEHICLES OR BICYCLES:
It shall be unlawful for any person owning or possessing any dog to permit such
dog to chase any motor vehicle or bicycle traveling upon any public or private
street or sidewalk. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-12: AUTHORITY TO TAKE UP DOGS RUNNING AT LARGE ON PRIVATE PROPERTY OR
PUBLIC PLACES:
Any person finding any dog running at large upon his property or upon any
premises enumerated in section
6-3-3-9 of this article to his injury or annoyance may take up such dog and
remove it or have it impounded. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-13: DANGEROUS DOGS:
It shall be unlawful for any person owning or possessing any dangerous dog to
permit such dangerous dog to run at large, whether such dog be muzzled or
unmuzzled. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-14: IMPOUNDING DANGEROUS DOGS:
Any dangerous dog running at large shall be taken up and impounded whenever
possible; provided, however, that if any police officer reasonably believes
that such dog in any way endangers any person, such official is authorized to
kill such dog. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-15: CRUELTY TO ANIMALS:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to instigate, cause, procure or
encourage any fight between animals, either in private or in public.
   (B)   It shall be unlawful for any person to hunt or attempt to kill by any
means any game animal or game birds within the city.
   (C)   It shall be unlawful for any person to treat any animal within the
city in any cruel manner whatsoever. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-16: DUTY UPON STRIKING ANIMAL WITH MOTOR VEHICLE:
It shall be unlawful for any person who kills or injures any animal while
driving a motor vehicle to leave the scene of the accident without first
stopping and rendering such assistance as is practical. Such person shall
immediately report the incident to the police department. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-17: INTENTIONAL INJURING OF ANIMALS:
In addition to the other prohibitions of this chapter, no person shall kill or
wound, or attempt to kill or wound, by any means whatsoever, any bird or
squirrel, or rob or injure the nest of such creatures, or enter upon any
private premises or public place, for the purpose of doing any act prohibited
by this section; provided, however, that this section shall not apply to crows,
starlings, hawks, sparrows and pigeons. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-18: PROCUREMENT OF ANIMAL WITHOUT KNOWLEDGE OF OWNER:
It shall be unlawful for any person in any manner to procure or acquire, or
attempt to procure or acquire, or knowingly cause or aid in the procurement or
acquisition of any animal for any purpose without the consent of the owner
thereof. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-19: ABANDONING ANIMALS WITHIN CITY:
It shall be unlawful for any owner or person in control of any animal to
abandon such animal within the city. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-20: KEEPING ANIMALS IN SANITARY CONDITION:
   (A)   Required: Every owner or person in possession of an animal shall
maintain their animal in a clean and sanitary condition.
   (B)   Adequate Shelter And Sustenance: Every owner or person in possession
of an animal shall provide adequate food, water and shelter. If sheltered
outside of a residence, the animal shelter shall conform to the following:
      1.   The shelter shall be of sufficient height and width to permit said
animal to stand up and turn around inside, when fully grown, for each animal.
      2.   Said shelter in which said animal or animals are confined shall
provide shade from the sun from ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. until four o'clock (4:
00) P.M. each day. (Ord. 06-04, 3-21-2006)
6-3-3-21: OFFENSIVE ODORS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to cause or permit offensive odors to
emanate from the premises where he keeps any animal. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-22: FEMALE DOGS IN HEAT:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person in possession of any female dog to
permit such female dog to run at large within the city at any time while such
dog is in heat.
   (B)   In addition to any penalty for which the owner shall be liable under
this chapter, such dog shall be impounded. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-23: USE OF ANIMALS FOR INDECENT PURPOSES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to in any manner instigate, cause, procure,
participate in or assist in any indecent, lewd or immoral show, use or
exhibition of an animal. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-24: CERTAIN ANIMALS PROHIBITED IN CITY:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to own, use, keep or permit to be
at large within the city any of the following animals: bees, pigeons, horses,
cattle, sheep, ponies, mules, goats, pigs, swine, hogs, ducks, geese, chickens,
minks, skunks, foxes or any other livestock or poultry or any wild or vicious
animal dangerous to mankind.
   (B)   Any animal named in subsection (A) of this section which is found at
large within the city shall be impounded, if possible; provided, however, that
whenever any police officers believe such animal endangers any person, such
animal may be killed by said officer.
   (C)   In addition to any other penalties imposed upon any person violating
this section, such person shall also be liable for the costs of impounding or
killing such animal, if necessary. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-25: DISEASED OR DYING ANIMALS; RUNNING AT LARGE:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful to allow any animal afflicted with any contagious
or infectious disease to run at large or to be exposed in any public place
whereby the health of persons or other animals may be affected; nor shall such
diseased animal be removed or shipped from the premises of the owner thereof
except under the supervision of the health officer or a licensed veterinarian.
   (B)   The health officer shall cause such disposition of any diseased animal
and such treatment of affected premises as to prevent the communication or
spread of contagion or infection.
   (C)   Whenever any animal is in any street or public place within the city
and appears, in the estimation of any police officer or health officer, to be
injured or diseased beyond recovery, and is not being attended to and properly
cared for by the owner or other proper person in control thereof, and whenever
such animal has not been removed to some private premises or other place
designated by such officer within one hour after being found or left in such
condition, such animal may be put to death by such officer or his authorized
agent and, unless at once removed by the owner, shall be treated as any other
dead animal found on a street or public place, as hereinafter provided. (1972
Code)
6-3-3-26: DEAD OR DYING ANIMALS; REMOVAL REQUIRED:
Any person possessing any dead animal injured or diseased beyond recovery,
which is not killed for meat or is improper for use as meat, or which is in an
offensive condition or sick with an infectious or contagious disease, shall at
once notify the health officer thereof, and upon the health officer's order,
such person, at his own expense, shall at once remove or cause the removal of
such animal. (1972 Code)
6-3-3-27: DEAD OR DYING ANIMALS; BURIAL, THROWING INTO STREETS, KEEPING:
It shall be unlawful for any person to abandon, deposit or throw upon any place
or street or public water, or to offensively expose or bury anywhere within the
city the body or any part thereof of any dead or fatally diseased or injured
animal; nor shall any person keep any dead animal or any offensive meat, bird,
fowl or fish in a place where the same may be dangerous to the life or
detrimental to the health of any person. (1972 Code)
ARTICLE IV. PENALTIES
6-3-4-1: LIABILITY OF OWNERS OR KEEPER; DAMAGE TO ANIMALS:
The owner or keeper of any animal shall be liable for all damages that may
accrue to any other person by reason of any such animal pursuing, chasing,
wounding or killing any animal belonging to such other person; provided,
however, that no owner or keeper of any animal shall be liable for any damage
caused by such animal having rabies or other similar disease unknown to such
owner or keeper. (1972 Code)
6-3-4-2: LIABILITY OF OWNERS OR KEEPER; INJURY TO PERSONS:
If an animal without provocation attacks or injures any person who is peaceably
conducting himself in any place where he may lawfully be, the owner or keeper
of such animal shall be liable in damages to the person so attacked or injured
to the full amount of the injury sustained. (1972 Code)
6-3-4-3: LIABILITY OF OWNERS OR KEEPER; DAMAGE TO PROPERTY:
The owner or keeper of an animal which damages or destroys any public or
private property shall be held liable for the full value of the property
damaged or destroyed. (1972 Code)
6-3-4-4: DANGEROUS ANIMALS:
In addition to any other penalty which may be imposed, any animal declared to
be a dangerous animal by a court of competent jurisdiction may be ordered by
the court to be muzzled, removed from the city limits or destroyed. (Ord. 00-
04, 4-4-2000)
CHAPTER 4
UNFAIR HOUSING
SECTION:
6-4-1: Definitions
6-4-2: Prohibited Acts
6-4-3: Fair Housing Board
6-4-4: Duties Of Fair Housing Board
6-4-5: Procedures
6-4-6: Penalty
6-4-7: Remedies
6-4-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, unless a different meaning clearly appears from the
context, the following terms shall have the meanings ascribed:
DISCRIMINATE: Includes difference in treatment in the sale, lease, rental or
financing of housing accommodations because of race, color, creed, religion,
religious beliefs or national origin.
HOUSING: Any building or structure, or portion thereof designed, intended,
arranged or designed to be used as or occupied as a home, residence, living
quarters or sleeping place of one or more human beings.
HOUSING ACCOMMODATION: Means and includes any building, structure or portion
thereof which is used or occupied, or is maintained, arranged or designated or
designed to be used or occupied as a home, residence or sleeping place of one
or more human beings.
LENDING INSTITUTION: Any bank, insurance company, savings and loan association
or person in the business of lending money or guaranteeing loans, or any person
in the business of obtaining, arranging or negotiating loans or guarantees as
an agent or broker, or any person in the business of buying or selling of loans
or instruments for the payment of money which is secured by title to or a
security interest in real estate.
OWNER: Any person who holds legal or equitable title to, or any beneficial
interest in, any dwelling or housing, or to any legal or equitable title to
shares of, or any beneficial interest in, any real estate cooperative which
owns any dwelling or housing.
REAL ESTATE BROKER: Any real estate broker or agent thereof or who exercises
any function of a real estate broker within the city. (1972 Code)
6-4-2: PROHIBITED ACTS:
It shall be an unfair housing practice and unlawful for any "real estate
broker", "lending institution", "owner" or person, as defined in section
6-4-1 of this chapter, to commit any of the following acts, or acts prohibited
because of or due to race, color, creed, religion, religious beliefs or
national origin:
   (A)   Refuse to show, sell, lease or rent any dwelling or housing solely
because of race, color, creed, religion, religious beliefs or national origin.
   (B)   Make any discriminations, distinction or restriction against any
purchaser or lessee in the showing, price, terms, conditions or privileges
relating to the sale, rental, lease or occupancy of any dwelling or housing, or
in the furnishing of any facilities or services in connection therewith.
   (C)   Cause any written or oral inquiry or record to be made concerning such
prohibited acts, or a person seeking to purchase, rent or lease any dwelling or
housing.
   (D)   Publish, circulate, issue or display, or cause to be published,
circulated, issued or displayed, any communication, notice, advertisement, sign
or other writing of any kind relating to the sale, rental or leasing of any
housing accommodation within the city which will indicate or express any
limitation or discrimination in the sale, rental or leasing of such housing
accommodation, of any prospective buyer, lessee or renter of such property.
   (E)   To solicit for sale, lease or listing for sale or lease, of any
housing accommodations within this city on the loss of value due to the present
or prospective entry into the neighborhood of any person or persons of any
particular race, color, creed, religion, religious beliefs or national origin.
   (F)   Distribute or cause to be distributed, written material or statements
designed to induce any owner of any housing accommodation to sell or lease his
property.
   (G)   Discriminate or to participate in discrimination in connection with
borrowing or lending money, guaranteeing loans, accepting mortgages or
otherwise obtaining or making available funds for the purchase, acquisition,
construction, rehabilitation, repair or maintenance of any housing
accommodation in the city.
   (H)   To exploit or overcharge any person for housing accommodations within
this city.
   (I)   To deliberately refuse examination of copies of listing of a
residential property or real estate within this city, or to accept and enter
into any limitation in such listing for causes above mentioned. (1972 Code)
6-4-3: FAIR HOUSING BOARD:
There is hereby created a fair housing board, which shall be appointed by the
mayor, and shall consist of five (5) members, to be approved by the city
council. The mayor shall designate one of its members to be chairperson. Any
three (3) members of said board shall constitute a quorum. The term of office
of each member shall be for three (3) years, or until his successor is
appointed and qualified. The mayor shall designate which of the two (2) first
appointed shall serve for two (2) year terms, and the remaining members,
including the chairperson, shall be appointed for three (3) year terms.
Thereafter, appointments shall be for the full three (3) year terms or for
unexpired terms in event of vacancy. (1972 Code)
6-4-4: DUTIES OF FAIR HOUSING BOARD:
It shall be the duty of the fair housing board to:
   (A)   Act to eliminate discriminatory practices as specified in section
6-4-2 of this chapter, and to initiate or receive and investigate complaints
charging unlawful housing practices;
   (B)   Seek conciliation of such complaints, hold public hearings, make
findings of fact, issue orders and publish its findings of fact and orders in
accordance with the provisions of this chapter;
   (C)   Render, from time to time but not less than every three (3) months, a
written report of its activities and recommendations with respect to fair
housing practices, to the mayor and city council; and
   (D)   Adopt such rules and regulations as may be necessary to carry out the
purposes of this chapter and the orderly handling of its business and duties.
(1972 Code)
6-4-5: PROCEDURES:
   (A)   Any person aggrieved in any manner by a violation of the provisions of
this chapter shall file a written complaint setting forth his grievance.
Complaints may be filed with the fair housing board by leaving the same with
the city clerk. Each complaint shall set forth the name and address of the
complainant, together with his telephone number; the name and address of the
person against whom the complaint is brought, and it shall state in detail the
alleged facts surrounding the alleged violation of this chapter. Any complaint
shall be filed, as aforesaid, within ninety (90) days after the alleged unfair
housing practice occurred, or it shall be barred.
   (B)   After the filing of any complaint, the chairperson of the fair housing
board shall designate two (2) members of said board to make a prompt
investigation in connection therewith; and if such members shall determine
after such investigation, that probable cause exists for crediting the
allegations of the complaint, they shall immediately endeavor to eliminate the
unlawful discriminatory practice complained of by conference, conciliation and
persuasion. In case of a determination that probable cause does not exist, the
fair housing board shall make written findings of fact and shall send copies
thereof to the complainant and the accused within twenty (20) days from the
date of such finding. If attempts at conciliation are not successful within
thirty (30) days after filing of the complaint, the board shall then proceed
promptly to a full hearing of the complaint.
   (C)   In case of the failure to so eliminate such unfair practice, or in
advance thereof, if in the judgment of the fair housing board the circumstances
so warrant, they may cause to be issued and served in the name of the fair
housing board, a written notice, together with a copy of such complaint, to all
parties, of a full hearing on the complaint at a time and place to be specified
in such notice. The notice shall be served on all parties not less than seven
(7) days before the time set for public hearing. The public hearing shall be
held not later than forty five (45) days from the date of the filing of the
complaint. A copy of the notice of public hearing shall be furnished the local
press.
   (D)   The accused shall have the right to file an answer to the complaint,
to appear at the hearing in person and/or to be represented by counsel, and to
examine witnesses and submit testimony. The complainant shall present testimony
in person and such evidence as he deems or is pertinent. He too, may be
represented by counsel.
   (E)   The fair housing board shall conduct all hearings, but shall not be
bound by the strict rules of evidence prevailing in courts of law or equity.
The fair housing board shall have full power to subpoena witnesses and
pertinent documents, which power may be enforced by said board by proper
petition to the circuit court of the eleventh judicial circuit at Logan County,
Illinois. The board, aforesaid, shall have power to administer oaths and to
take sworn testimony. At the conclusion of the hearing, the board shall render
a written report and recommendations, within ten (10) days, which shall be
served by mail upon the parties. Hearings may be continued from time to time,
but shall be heard and concluded within sixty (60) days from the date of the
first hearing. (1972 Code)
6-4-6: PENALTY:
If, upon the due consideration of all evidence produced at the hearing, the
fair housing board finds that the person against whom the complaint has been
filed has engaged in or is engaging in an unfair housing practice, as defined
in this chapter, the board shall state its finding of fact and shall issue and
cause to be served upon such person an order requiring such person or the
accused to cease and desist from such unfair housing practice and it shall take
such affirmative or other action as, in the judgment of the fair housing board,
will effectuate the purposes of this chapter, including the requirement of a
report of the manner of compliance. The board shall retain jurisdiction of the
case until it is satisfied that the accused has complied with the order. In the
event that the board determines that the accused has not complied with its
orders, it shall be empowered to recommend to the city council for authority to
have the city attorney do any one of the following:
   (A)   Institute and prosecute proceedings to enforce against the accused
found guilty in the violation of this chapter a fine as hereinafter provided.
   (B)   To apply to any court of competent jurisdiction:
      1.   For an order restraining such person from violating any provision of
this chapter;
      2.   For such other or further relief as may seem to the court
appropriate for the enforcement of this chapter and the elimination of
violation hereof.
   (C)   Any person violating any of the provisions of this chapter may, upon
conviction thereof, be fined not less than ten dollars ($10.00) and not more
than five hundred dollars ($500.00), plus costs, and each day the violation
continues shall be a separate offense and subject to fine for each said
violation, separately. However, such fine shall not be a limitation upon nor a
consent, or prevent to also use one or more of the other remedies available
hereunder. (1972 Code)
6-4-7: REMEDIES:
Any person aggrieved by the violation of any provision of this chapter who has
exhausted the remedies provided for in this chapter may apply to any court of
competent jurisdiction for appropriate relief from such violation, including:
   (A)   An order compelling compliance with this chapter;
   (B)   An order to prohibit any person found by the court to have violated
any provision of this chapter for the sale, lease, exchange, transfer,
conveyance or assignment of any dwelling or housing which is subject to such
violation;
   (C)   An order requiring specific performance of any contract for the sale,
lease, exchange, transfer, conveyance or assignment of any dwelling or housing
by any person who is violating this chapter or has violated this chapter or
refuses to perform for one of the reasons herein prohibited as an unfair
practice;
   (D)   Compensatory damages; and
   (E)   Such other and further relief as may seem to the court appropriate for
the enforcement of this chapter and the elimination of the violation hereof.
(1972 Code)
TITLE 7
HEALTH AND SANITATION
CHAPTER 1
NUISANCES
SECTION:
   Article I. In General
7-1-1-1: Nuisances Declared Unlawful
7-1-1-2: Nuisance Defined, Generally
7-1-1-3: Nuisances Not Enumerated Herein
7-1-1-4: Enumeration Not Exclusive
7-1-1-5: Duty Of City Officers To Investigate; Power Of Entry
7-1-1-6: Notice To Proper Officials
   Article II. Certain Nuisances Declared
7-1-2-1: Foul Odors, Filth
7-1-2-2: Rubbish, Dry Grass
7-1-2-3: Weeds
7-1-2-4: Petroleum Products, Explosives
7-1-2-5: Unsafe Buildings
7-1-2-6: Abandoned Refrigerators
7-1-2-7: Junk
7-1-2-8: Inoperable Motor Vehicles, Equipment
7-1-2-9: Dust, Cinders
7-1-2-10: Scaffolding, Ladders
   Article III. Abatement
7-1-3-1: Notice To Abate Nuisance
7-1-3-2: Abatement Of Nuisances; City To Abate; Time Limits
7-1-3-3: Failure To Abate, Separate And Recurring Offense
7-1-3-4: Abatement By City
7-1-3-5: Summary Abatement By City When Emergency Or On Public Property
7-1-3-6: Costs Of Abatement; Debt Of Owner
ARTICLE I. IN GENERAL
7-1-1-1: NUISANCES DECLARED UNLAWFUL:
It shall be unlawful and a violation of this chapter for any person to wilfully
or negligently create, erect, maintain or permit a nuisance to exist anywhere
within the city. (1972 Code)
7-1-1-2: NUISANCE DEFINED, GENERALLY:
Any thing, act, omission, occupation or condition which shall exist or continue
for such length of time as to:
   (A)   Substantially annoy, injure or endanger the health, safety, peace or
welfare of the public; or
   (B)   In any way render the public insecure in life or property; or
   (C)   Greatly offend the public morals or decency; or
   (D)   Unlawfully and substantially interfere with, obstruct or render
dangerous for passage any street, sidewalk, alley, navigable body or other
public way or place;
is hereby declared a nuisance. (1972 Code)
7-1-1-3: NUISANCES NOT ENUMERATED HEREIN:
Any nuisance declared by statute, this chapter or other provisions of this code
or ordinances of the city shall be enforceable under the provisions of this
chapter as if enumerated specifically herein. (1972 Code)
7-1-1-4: ENUMERATION NOT EXCLUSIVE:
Nuisances enumerated in this chapter shall not be deemed exclusive, but are in
addition to and to be construed in conjunction with any other nuisances
enumerated in statutes or other provisions of this code or ordinances of the
city. (1972 Code)
7-1-1-5: DUTY OF CITY OFFICERS TO INVESTIGATE; POWER OF ENTRY:
   (A)   For the purpose of discovering nuisances, it shall be the duty of
police, fire, health and building officers and inspectors to investigate,
confirm and report any nuisances coming to their attention.
   (B)   In order to investigate, confirm and report nuisances, said officers
and inspectors shall, upon proper identification, be permitted, at any
reasonable hour and in a reasonable manner, to visit and enter into or upon any
premises or property within the city to make an examination thereof, if they
shall have reasonable grounds to believe that a nuisance exists. (1972 Code)
7-1-1-6: NOTICE TO PROPER OFFICIALS:
Whenever any nuisance shall be reported to or investigated and determined by
the police, fire, health or building officers or inspectors, notice shall be
given to the owner or person in control of the property or premises involved,
and to the appropriate city officials whose functions include the abatement of
such nuisances. (1972 Code)
ARTICLE II. CERTAIN NUISANCES DECLARED
7-1-2-1: FOUL ODORS, FILTH:
It is hereby declared to be a nuisance and a danger to the health, safety,
welfare, peace and comfort of the city and its residents for any person:
   (A)   Businesses: To conduct any business or to use any premises so as to
create an offensive or foul odor which taints the air and renders it nauseous
to persons in the vicinity; or
   (B)   Animals: To keep or maintain any animals in an unclean or filthy
manner or surroundings, or to keep or maintain any animals from which emit any
particularly foul or offensive odors; or
   (C)   Animal Carcasses: To cause or permit to be collected or to remain upon
any premises or place any animal carcass or any offal, filth, excretion or
other noisome or noxious animal matter of any kind which is, or is likely to
become, putrid, foul or offensive; or
   (D)   Vegetable Matter: To cause or permit to be collected or to remain upon
any premises or place any slop or other vegetable matter of any kind which is,
or is likely to become, putrid, foul or offensive; or
   (E)   Cellars, Vaults, Privies: To cause or permit any cellar, vault,
cistern, drain, privy, yard or other premises whatsoever to become, from any
cause, foul or offensive or injurious to the public health; or
   (F)   Stagnant Water: To permit to be collected or to stand upon any
premises any foul or stagnant water of any kind; or
   (G)   Stables And Pigsties: To locate or maintain, or permit to exist or
remain, anywhere within the city any stable or pigsty; or
   (H)   Foul Or Noxious Substances: To use, deposit or keep any property,
substance or thing emitting or causing any foul, offensive, noisome, nauseous
or noxious odor, effluvia or stench particularly repulsive to the physical
senses and which annoys, discomforts or endangers the welfare, health or safety
of any person. (1972 Code)
7-1-2-2: RUBBISH, DRY GRASS:
It is hereby declared a menace to the public safety and health and a nuisance
for any person to cause or permit:
   (A)   Rubbish, Rags: The deposit or accumulation of any refuse, oily rags,
rubbish or other materials or substances of any kind, so as to constitute a
fire hazard; or
   (B)   Dry Grass, Vegetation: The deposit, accumulation, existence or growth
upon any property of any dry or dead weeds, grass, vegetation or other like
substances of any kind, so as to constitute a fire hazard. (1972 Code)
7-1-2-3: WEEDS:
It is hereby declared a menace to the public safety and health and a nuisance
for any person to cause or permit:
   (A)   Jimson, Burdock: Any weeds, such as jimson, burdock, ragweed, thistle,
cockleburs, or other weeds of a like kind, to grow in any lot or tract of land
in the city.
   (B)   Height: Any weeds, grass or plants, other than trees, bushes, flowers,
vegetables or other ornamental plants, to grow to a height exceeding eight
inches (8") anywhere in the city.
   (C)   Barberry Bushes: Growth of the bush of the tall, common or European
barberry, further known as Berberis vulgaris or its horticultural varieties,
within the city. (1972 Code)
7-1-2-4: PETROLEUM PRODUCTS, EXPLOSIVES:
It is hereby declared a menace to the public safety and a nuisance for any
person to cause or permit:
   (A)   Petroleum Products: The accumulation or storage, within one hundred
(100) yards of any building occupied as a residence or business, other than a
licensed gasoline service station, of any petroleum, naphtha, benzine, coal
oil, gasoline, kerosene, turpentine or other petroleum products or inflammable
substances of any kind, in quantities greater than fifty (50) gallons; or
   (B)   Explosives: The deposit, accumulation, storage or presence, within one
hundred (100) yards of any building occupied as a residence or business, of any
powder magazine, nitroglycerine, dynamite or other explosive substance of any
kind. (1972 Code)
7-1-2-5: UNSAFE BUILDINGS:
   (A)   Prohibition: It is hereby declared a menace to the public safety and a
nuisance for any person to cause or permit the existence of any unsafe,
dilapidated or otherwise insecure building, wall, stack, chimney, cornice,
sign, awning or other like structure of any kind which, from manner of
construction, age, condition or other circumstances, is or may become a menace
to the safety of persons or property.
   (B)   Unsafe Building Defined: The term "unsafe building", as used herein,
is hereby defined to mean and include: 1) any building, shed, fence or other
manmade structure which is dangerous to the public health because of its
construction or condition, or which may cause or aid in the spread of disease
or cause injury to the health of the occupants of it or of neighboring
structures; 2) any building, shed, fence or other manmade structure which,
because of faulty construction, age, lack of proper repair or any other cause,
is especially liable to fire, and constitutes or creates a fire hazard; 3) any
building, shed, fence or other manmade structure which, by reason of faulty
construction, age, lack of proper repair or any other cause, is liable to cause
injury or damage by collapsing or by a collapse or fall of any part of such a
structure; or 4) any building, shed, fence or other manmade structure which,
because of its condition or because of lack of doors or windows is available to
and frequented by malefactors or disorderly persons who are not lawful
occupants of such structure.
   (C)   Notice: If any building shall be found in a dangerous and unsafe
condition, the mayor or any official or employee designated by the city council
shall notify in writing the owner or owners thereof, directing said owner or
owners to put such building in a safe condition or to demolish it. Where, upon
diligent search, the identity or whereabouts of the owner or owners of any such
building shall not be ascertainable, such notice shall be mailed to the person
or persons in whose name such real estate was last assessed.
   (D)   Failure To Comply: If, after fifteen (15) days subsequent to the
giving of such notice, said owner or owners fail to put such building in a safe
condition or to demolish it, the mayor or any official or employee designated
by the city council shall so notify the city council, requesting the council to
direct the city attorney to apply on behalf of the city to the circuit court of
Logan County for an order authorizing the city to demolish or repair, or to
cause the demolition or repair of said building.
   (E)   Cost Recovery: The cost of such demolition or repair shall be
recoverable from the owner or owners of such real estate, and shall be a lien
thereon as provided in 65 Illinois Compiled Statutes section 5/11-31-1, as
amended. (1972 Code)
7-1-2-6: ABANDONED REFRIGERATORS:
It is hereby declared a menace to the public safety and a nuisance for any
person to cause or permit the existence or storage in any place accessible to
children of any abandoned or discarded refrigerator, icebox, ice chest, deep
freeze or other airtight appliance or container of any kind, of a capacity of
one and one-half (11/2) cubic feet or more, from which the lids, doors or other
covers have not been removed or which cannot easily be opened by a child, by
means of pushing only, from the inside thereof. (1972 Code)
7-1-2-7: JUNK:
It is declared to be a danger to public health and safety and a nuisance for
any person to store, keep or maintain outside of a closed building any junk,
parts, machinery or equipment unless the premises upon which the same are
maintained is a properly licensed junkyard. (Ord. 86-12, 5-20-1986)
7-1-2-8: INOPERABLE MOTOR VEHICLES, EQUIPMENT:
   (A)   No person, whether as owner or lessee of a motor vehicle, or owner or
otherwise in charge of premises within the city, shall park or locate, or
permit the parking or location of, an inoperable motor vehicle or parts
thereof, for more than seven (7) days outside of a garage or other enclosed
building on any real property zoned for residential use or upon public
property. At no time shall any vehicle of any type undergo disassembly of parts
commonly called "stripping", or a major overhaul, including body work, on such
property outside of a garage or other enclosed building. This section shall not
apply to any motor vehicle located within a building when not in use, to any
vehicle registered and licensed with the state as an antique vehicle, or to a
motor vehicle on the premises of a place of business engaged in the wrecking or
junking of motor vehicles or machinery. (Ord. 00-04-1, 6-6-2000)
   (B)   "Inoperable motor vehicle" means any motor vehicle from which the
engine, wheels or other parts have been removed, or on which the engine, wheels
or other parts have been altered, damaged or otherwise so treated as to render
the vehicle incapable of being safely driven under its own motor power; and
such definition also includes an unlicensed or unregistered motor vehicle,
whether or not mechanically operable; provided, however, that this definition
shall not be construed to include any motor vehicle which has been rendered
temporarily incapable of being driven under its own power in order to perform
ordinary service or repair operations. (Ord. 88-10, 2-2-1988)
7-1-2-9: DUST, CINDERS:
   (A)   It is hereby declared a menace to the public health and a nuisance for
any person to cause or permit any operations that cause or permit any dirt,
sand, gravel, cinders, ashes, earth or other similar materials to be hauled,
moved, rolled, compacted, scraped, dragged or otherwise disturbed so as to
cause or permit dust to be raised, blown or stirred through the operation of
machinery or otherwise to the detriment of any person or property.
   (B)   Every person engaged in hauling any sand, dirt, cinders, ashes, earth
or other similar materials or substances, or engaged in the moving, rolling,
compacting, scraping, dragging or other disturbance of soil and the like, shall
make adequate provision as often as is required to arrest and prevent such dust
through the use of salts, oil, chemicals and other materials used and
recommended for retarding or eliminating such dust, subject to the supervision
and approval of the director of public works. (1972 Code)
7-1-2-10: SCAFFOLDING, LADDERS:
It is hereby declared a menace to the public safety and a nuisance for any
person:
   (A)   To erect or use, or to cause or permit to be erected or used, any
insecure or unsafe scaffold or ladder whereby the safety of persons working
thereon or passing thereunder may in any way be endangered.
   (B)   To place or leave, or to cause or permit to be placed or left, any
tools or articles on any such scaffold or ladder in such manner that the same
may fall into any street, sidewalk or other public way, whereby the safety of
persons passing thereunder may in any way be endangered. (1972 Code)
ARTICLE III. ABATEMENT
7-1-3-1: NOTICE TO ABATE NUISANCE:
   (A)   Required: Whenever any health or building official or inspector, or
any police or fire officer, determines that a nuisance exists on any private
property or premises, except as otherwise provided herein, the proper city
official shall cause a written notice to be served personally upon the owner
or, if the owner cannot be found, upon the occupant or person in control of the
property or premises who is causing, permitting or maintaining such nuisance,
and shall cause a copy of said notice to be conspicuously posted within or upon
such property or premises.
   (B)   Content: Such notice shall fairly apprise such person of the nature of
the nuisance, his duty to abate or remove the nuisance within the time provided
therein, the penalty for failure to abate the same, and shall state that, if
said nuisance is abated by the city, liability for necessary expenses so
incurred shall accrue as provided for in section 7-1-3-6 of this article. (1972
Code)
7-1-3-2: ABATEMENT OF NUISANCES; CITY TO ABATE; TIME LIMITS:
It is hereby declared the duty of any person determined to have created,
caused, erected, maintained or permitted a nuisance to exist within the city to
discontinue and abate such nuisance within forty eight (48) hours or such other
time period as may be specified therein, from the time he receives written
notice thereof. (1972 Code)
7-1-3-3: FAILURE TO ABATE, SEPARATE AND RECURRING OFFENSE:
It shall be unlawful and a violation of this chapter for any person to neglect,
refuse or otherwise fail to remove or abate any nuisance after expiration of
the forty eight (48) hour or other specified time period provided by notice
thereof; and each twenty four (24) hours, or fraction thereof, during which
such nuisance continues or exists shall be deemed a separate offense. (1972
Code)
7-1-3-4: ABATEMENT BY CITY:
Whenever any nuisance is not abated by the owner, lessee or person in control
of premises or property affected within the time provided by notice, the proper
city officer shall cause the abatement or removal of such nuisance. (1972 Code)
7-1-3-5: SUMMARY ABATEMENT BY CITY WHEN EMERGENCY OR ON PUBLIC PROPERTY:
Whenever any nuisance: a) constitutes or is deemed to be an imminent or
immediate danger to public health or safety; or b) exists on public property,
the proper city officer shall cause such nuisance to be summarily and
immediately abated and removed, regardless of any forty eight (48) hour or
other time period specified by notice to the person responsible therefor;
provided, however, that in situation a) of this section, such officer shall
have first applied for and obtained the written permission of the mayor for
such summary abatement. (1972 Code)
7-1-3-6: COSTS OF ABATEMENT; DEBT OF OWNER:
   (A)   Any costs or expenses of abatement reasonably incurred by the city
pursuant to the provisions of sections
7-1-3-4 and
7-1-3-5 of this article shall be deemed a debt to the city by the owner, lessee
or person in control of premises upon which such nuisance existed; provided,
that where specifically provided in this code or by statute, such costs and
expenses shall become a lien upon the real estate or personal property
affected, superior to all other liens and encumbrances, except tax liens.
   (B)   It shall be the duty of the city attorney to enforce by civil action
any and all such debts of liens as provided in subsection (A) of this section.
(1972 Code)

ARTICLE I. DEFINITIONS
7-3-1-1: TERMS DEFINED:
The following words and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the
meaning given to them in this article unless the context clearly indicates
otherwise:
ASHES: Residue from fires used for cooking or heating buildings, or disposing
of landscape waste.
BRUSH: Trimmings from shrubs, trees or other woody plants not less than two
feet (2') or more than six feet (6') in length.
GARBAGE: Wastes resulting from the handling, packaging, preparation, cooking or
consumption of food.
REFUSE: Garbage, rubbish, ashes, bulky wastes, brush, construction and
demolition wastes, and other wastes.
REFUSE COLLECTOR: A person, firm, or corporation which, for a fee, collects
refuse in the city.
RUBBISH: Combustibles such as paper, cardboard cartons, wood pallets, wood,
boxes, excelsior, plastic, rags, cloth, bedding, leather, rubber, or
noncombustibles such as metal, tin cans, metal foil, dirt, stone, bricks,
ceramics, crockery, glass, bottles or combinations thereof weighing thirty five
(35) pounds or less.
WASTES, BULKY: Individual items of furniture, equipment, or machinery or parts
thereof weighing more than thirty five (35) pounds, but less than five hundred
(500) pounds, including, as illustrative examples, the following: auto parts,
tires and wheels, mechanical equipment, TV sets, stoves, refrigerators,
furniture pieces, individual items which but for their weight would constitute
rubbish, individual items of construction and demolition waste, freezers,
clothes washers, clothes dryers, dishwashers, trash compactors, water heaters,
furnaces, carpeting, bed mattresses, bed box springs, powered lawn mowers, etc.
WASTES, CONSTRUCTION AND DEMOLITION: Any lumber, plywood, paneling, plastic
board, roofing scraps, sheeting scraps, plastic, glass, concrete, rubble,
conduit, pipe, wire, or other wastes generated from the construction,
remodeling, repair, or demolition of the building, dwelling, structure or
portion thereof.
WASTES, OTHER: Any item not specifically otherwise enumerated in this article.
(Ord. 90-08, 7-3-1990)
ARTICLE II. REQUIREMENTS FOR REFUSE COLLECTION AND
   DISPOSAL FOR ONE- OR TWO-FAMILY DWELLING UNITS
7-3-2-0: USE OF COLLECTOR:
Any owner or occupant of a dwelling unit in a one- or two- family dwelling
shall utilize a refuse collector and shall do so in the following sections in
this article. (Ord. 90-08, 7-3-1990)
7-3-2-1: PREPARATION OF GARBAGE, RUBBISH, CONSTRUCTION AND DEMOLITION WASTES,
BULKY WASTES AND ASHES:
   (A)   All garbage shall be thoroughly drained of all liquid.
   (B)   Any sharp object constituting rubbish or construction or demolition
waste shall be securely wrapped in paper.
   (C)   Ashes shall be extinguished so that no hot coal or fire remains.
   (D)   No ashes shall be mixed with garbage, rubbish, construction or
demolition waste or brush. (Ord. 90-08, 7-3-1990)
7-3-2-2: RECEPTACLES:
   (A)   Standards: Except as provided in section
7-3-2-3 of this article, all garbage, rubbish, ashes and individual items of
construction and demolition waste, after being prepared in the manner required
by section
7-3-2-1 of this article, shall be placed in a refuse receptacle meeting the
following requirements and shall be placed for collection at the time and
location provided in subsection
7-3-2-3(A) of this article:
      1.   Approved Receptacles: Receptacles shall be constructed of galvanized
metal, aluminum, plastic, or other water and weatherproof material. They shall
taper from top to bottom, be fitted with handles or bales, and be equipped with
a cover or lid. Plastic bags of at least one and one-half (1.5) mil thickness
tied at the top, may be used. Total capacity of any receptacle shall not exceed
thirty (30) gallons (30 cubic feet) and a total weight of the receptacle and
contents thereof shall not exceed thirty five (35) pounds; however, mobile
carts of up to ninety (90) gallons' capacity shall be approved receptacles
hereunder if the same are designed for mechanical dumping and the refuse
collector accepts such receptacles.
      2.   Prohibited Containers: Prohibited containers shall include, but not
be limited to, metal drums, fiber or paperboard drums, wire trash burners,
barrels, paper shopping bags, cardboard boxes, receptacles without lids, open
plastic bags, or containers having sharp or jagged exposures.
   (B)   Responsibility For Maintenance: It is the joint obligation of the
owner and occupant of any dwelling unit in a one- or two-family dwelling
desiring to utilize the refuse collection and disposal service to provide
approved refuse containers and maintain same in good repair. Whenever any
receptacle shall become defective, it is the responsibility of the owner or
occupant to repair or replace same.
   (C)   Procedure For Disposal Of Defective Receptacles: The city or the
refuse collector shall have the right to condemn any defective receptacle by
placing thereon a red tag or sticker which shall be notice to the owner or
occupant of its defective nature. The owner of such receptacle shall replace or
repair the same before it is used again and the city or collector shall have
the right to dispose of the defective receptacle during any subsequent
collection. (Ord. 90-08, 7-3-1990)
7-3-2-3: PLACEMENT OF RECEPTACLES:
   (A)   Time And Location: Not earlier than six o'clock (6:00) P.M. of the day
preceding collection, any owner, operator or occupant of a one- or two-family
dwelling utilizing a refuse collector shall place or cause to be placed
approved receptacles, at the street side, behind the pavement surface line, so
placed that the contents will not be scattered by the wind or animals.
Receptacles shall be returned to the premises within twelve (12) hours after
having been emptied. No alley pick ups will be made.
   (B)   Quantities: The weekly refuse service shall include collection of the
contents of receptacles meeting the requirements of subsection
7-3-2-2(A)1 of this article, except in the case of approved plastic bags, in
which case, both the contents and the receptacle shall be collected. (Ord. 90-
08, 7-3-1990)
ARTICLE III. REQUIREMENTS FOR REFUSE COLLECTION AND
   DISPOSAL FOR OTHER THAN ONE- AND TWO-FAMILY DWELLING UNITS
7-3-3-1: OWNERS' OBLIGATION AND SPECIFICATIONS:
The owners of business, commercial, manufacturing, industrial, mobile home
parks, or residential structures and all other collection sites, other than
one- or two-family dwellings, in which refuse is accumulated for disposal,
shall provide or cause to be provided refuse receptacles meeting the following
requirements and shall collect or have collected said refuse at least on a
weekly basis and shall further provide for private refuse collection of the
contents thereof. Such owners shall provide:
   (A)   Refuse Bins: (Referred to from time to time in this chapter as
"dumpsters".) Those first placed in service after the effective date hereof,
shall meet or exceed the standards, rules and regulations of the Consumer
Product Safety Commission and particularly those regulations promulgated in
title 16, chapter 2, subchapter B, part 1301 as published in the Monday, June
13, 1977, Federal Register, page 30296, volume 42, number 113. All others
(being refuse bins currently in service) shall be securely fastened with safety
chains to permanently fixed objects to prevent them from tipping over.
   (B)   Roll-Off Boxes: Open metal attachable containers commonly known and
referred to herein as "roll-off boxes"; provided, however, such roll-off boxes
shall not be used for the storage or disposal of garbage, rubbish or other
refuse, the accumulation of which in such an open container would constitute a
nuisance, cause an offensive odor, or be difficult because the contents would
be scattered by the wind.
   (C)   Exceptions: When the use of a dumpster or roll-off box would otherwise
be required and where conditions exist which would make the use of such a
device impossible or impractical, the city may permit the use of other
receptacles. Any person desiring to utilize a receptacle other than a dumpster
or roll-off box where the use of one would otherwise be required shall submit a
written application to the city specifying the nature of the impossibility or
impracticality and describing the proposed type of receptacle. The mayor, with
city council consent, may condition his approval in writing as necessary to
provide a safe and sanitary refuse disposal procedure. (Ord. 90-08, 7-3-1990)
7-3-3-2: LOCATION OF RECEPTACLES:
   (A)   Dumpsters: Dumpsters shall not be permitted in the front yard or in
the front or side yard on corner lots. Dumpsters located within twenty five
feet (25') of a dedicated public street shall be screened from view at all
times.
   (B)   Roll-Off Boxes: Roll-off boxes shall not be permitted in a front yard
or on a dedicated street right of way; provided, however, the mayor may issue
temporary permission for a roll- off box to be located on the public right of
way or the mayor may issue temporary permission for a roll-off box to be placed
in a required front or side yard.
   (C)   Other Receptacles: Other receptacles shall be placed and stored as
specified by approval received from the mayor.
   (D)   Exceptions: Any person desiring to locate a dumpster or roll-off box
on the dedicated public right of way in a yard where the placement of such a
receptacle would otherwise be prohibited, other than temporarily, may submit a
request to the mayor specifying the proposed location, justifying the location,
and detailing how the receptacle will be screened so as to shelter and protect
surrounding properties to the same or a greater extent than if the receptacle
were located in a yard where it would otherwise be permitted. (Ord. 90-08, 7-3-
1990)
ARTICLE IV. DEPOSITING OR STORAGE OF REFUSE
7-3-4-1: DEPOSITING OR PERMITTING REFUSE TO REMAIN:
It shall be unlawful for any person to deposit, bury, throw, place or cause to
be deposited, buried, thrown or placed any refuse within the corporate limits
of the city. It shall be unlawful for any property owner, lessee, or tenant to
permit any refuse placed, deposited, buried, or thrown on any property owned,
leased, used, occupied, or in which such person otherwise has an interest to
remain on such property after such material has been placed, deposited, buried
or thrown thereon. Notwithstanding anything herein contained to the contrary,
any and all hazardous wastes, as defined by federal or state law, shall be
disposed of strictly in conformity with all state and federal rules and
regulations pertaining thereto. (Ord. 90-08, 7-3-1990)
7-3-4-2: STORAGE OR DISPOSAL OF REFUSE:
   (A)   Burning Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any person to burn or set
fire to or cause to be burned or cause to set fire to any refuse within the
city unless such material shall be burned in an incinerator or furnace properly
constructed for such purpose and approved by the environmental protection
agency.
   (B)   Requirements As To Storage Of Food: It shall be unlawful for any
person to store human or animal food or feed within the city limits in other
than a rat free and ratproof container, compartment or building.
   (C)   Refuse Placed Out For Collection In Violation Of This Chapter: It
shall be unlawful for any person to place out for collection, or cause to be
placed out for collection, any refuse within the corporate limits of the city
in a manner violating any provision of this chapter.
   (D)   Refuse Placed Out For Collection On Street Medians: It shall be
unlawful for any person to place out for collection or cause to be placed out
for collection any refuse on any street median within the city. (Ord. 90-08, 7-
3-1990)
ARTICLE V. PENALTY
7-3-5-1: PENALTY:
Any person found guilty of violating, disobeying, neglecting or refusing to
comply with or resisting or opposing the enforcement of any of the provisions
of this chapter, except when otherwise specifically provided, upon conviction
thereof, shall be fined not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than two
hundred dollars ($200.00) for each offense. A separate and distinct offense
shall be regarded as committed each day upon which said person shall continue
any such violation or permit any such violation to exist. (Ord. 90-08, 7-3-
1990)
ARTICLE VI. SOLID WASTE
7-3-6-1: ADOPTION OF COUNTY ORDINANCE:
The city hereby adopts the Logan County solid waste license ordinance and its
amendments, a copy of which is on file in the office of the city clerk, and the
same is hereby adopted and incorporated as fully as if set out at length
herein. (Ord. 98-17, 9-1-1998)
TITLE 8
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS, PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
8-1-1: Obstruct Streets; Building Materials
8-1-2: Moving Buildings Across, Through Streets
8-1-3: Steps Extending On Streets, Sidewalks
8-1-4: Encroachments; Removal
8-1-5: Merchandise On Sidewalks
8-1-6: Wagons, Goods On Streets; Removal
8-1-7: Interfere With Stakes
8-1-8: Throwing Debris On Streets
8-1-9: Coals, Fires On Streets
8-1-10: Traction Engines
8-1-11: Wagons, Animals; Driving On Public Ways
8-1-12: Obstructing Sidewalks
8-1-13: Water Drainage Prohibited
8-1-14: Railroads Obstructing Passage
8-1-15: Leaving Obstructions Prohibited
8-1-16: Permission To Construct Sidewalk
8-1-17: Strips For Lawns Permitted
8-1-18: Uniform Width Of Parkings
8-1-19: Driving On Parkings
8-1-20: Disturb Vehicles
8-1-21: Datum Plane
8-1-22: Trees, Planting Along Streets
8-1-23: Paved And/Or Asphalted Driveways
8-1-24: Rural Route Mailboxes
8-1-1: OBSTRUCT STREETS; BUILDING MATERIALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to encumber or obstruct any street, alley
or sidewalk with building or other like materials without having obtained a
written permit from the mayor or city council, except in cases of urgent
necessity and for a short time only, or to allow any obstruction that he may by
himself or by agent have made, to continue in any case longer than may be
necessary in the diligent erection of such building or the prompt execution of
the work. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-2: MOVING BUILDINGS ACROSS, THROUGH STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to remove or cause to be removed, or aid in
removing any building through or across any street or alley, without having
first obtained a written permit from the mayor or city council. No person shall
unnecessarily encumber or obstruct any alley or street for a longer time than
is necessary in the prompt and diligent removal of such building. (Ord. 11, 2-
6-1917)
8-1-3: STEPS EXTENDING ON STREETS, SIDEWALKS:
No steps, platform or other fixture shall be built to extend into or upon any
sidewalk or alley. No cellar way or basement way shall extend into or upon any
street or sidewalk more than three feet six inches (3'6"), nor into or upon any
alley more than four feet (4'). No cellar window or coal hole shall be placed
in any street, sidewalk or alley unless well secured by an iron grating or some
similar cover. Every cellar door and grating provided for in this section shall
be laid even with the grade of the sidewalk, street or alley where situated.
(Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-4: ENCROACHMENTS; REMOVAL:
   (A)   No person shall make or cause to be made any erection or enclosure
encroaching in whole or in part upon any street, alley or sidewalk. If any
erection or enclosure encroaching upon any street or alley on the effective
date hereof, shall not be removed within ten (10) days after the owner thereof
being notified by an officer of the city to remove such erection or enclosure,
such owner shall be subject to penalty as provided by section
1-4-1 of this code.
   (B)   No fixture, building, fence or other erection, encroachment or
enclosure now extending or encroaching upon any sidewalk, street or alley
contrary to the provisions hereof shall be repaired or rebuilt. (Ord. 11, 2-6-
1917)
8-1-5: MERCHANDISE ON SIDEWALKS:
No person shall encumber or obstruct more than four feet (4') of the outer edge
of the sidewalk with any goods, wares, merchandise, fuel or other articles or
property he may be receiving or delivering, nor shall he permit the same to
remain upon any sidewalk longer than may be necessary in the diligent removal
thereof, or in any case not longer than twenty four (24) hours. (Ord. 11, 2-6-
1917)
8-1-6: WAGONS, GOODS ON STREETS; REMOVAL:
   (A)   It shall be unlawful for any person to encumber any street, alley or
sidewalk or public grounds with wagons, mobile homes, motor vehicles, vehicles,
structures, barrels, boxes, lumber, timber, firewood, signs or any other
obstruction, or to place, throw or leave, or cause to be placed, thrown or left
any obstruction or encumbrance not authorized by ordinance in any street or
alley.
   (B)   The mayor or street commissioner may cause the removal of any
obstruction or encroachment upon any street or alley or sidewalk, and the costs
of such removal may be collected from the person causing or owning such
obstruction, with the penalty, or in a separate suit in the name of the city.
(Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-7: INTERFERE WITH STAKES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to purposely change or remove any stake,
post or stone set or placed to designate the corner or line of any lot or land,
street or alley, or to show the grade of any street, alley or sidewalk. (Ord.
11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-8: THROWING DEBRIS ON STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw, place, sweep or leave any paper,
grass from lawns, straw, ashes, dirt, filth, brush or other like substance, or
to cause the same to be thrown, placed, swept or left in or upon any street,
alley or sidewalk. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-9: COALS, FIRES ON STREETS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to throw, place or leave any live coals or
fire upon any planked street, alley, sidewalk or planked street crossing. (Ord.
11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-10: TRACTION ENGINES:
Any and all parties operating or running any tractor or engine in or upon any
of the streets or alleys of the city shall, in crossing a paved street or any
crossing in the city, use and employ planks, of such width and thickness
necessary to sustain the weight of such tractor or engine, to be placed on or
over such crossing and in such a manner that the wheels of such tractor or
engine shall run over the crossing on such planks. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-11: WAGONS, ANIMALS; DRIVING ON PUBLIC WAYS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to push, draw or run any buggy, sleigh,
wagon or other heavy vehicle, or drive, lead or ride any team or beast of
burden over or upon any paved or planked sidewalk, unless it may be necessary
in crossing the same to get into his premises, or into premises where no wagon
crossing or other suitable access is provided. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-12: OBSTRUCTING SIDEWALKS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct any street crossing by
unnecessarily stopping thereon with any team, vehicle, automobile or animal or
to fasten or leave any automobile or other vehicle or team or single animal so
that either of them obstructs the sidewalk or renders passage there along
unsafe, and to hinder persons desiring to use such crossing or sidewalk. (Ord.
11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-13: WATER DRAINAGE PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to permit the water to fall or drain from
any building owned by him, or under his control, to spread over the sidewalk or
front thereof. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-14: RAILROADS OBSTRUCTING PASSAGE:
No railroad company or conductor, engineer or other employee of any railroad
company, or other person moving or controlling any locomotive engine, car or
train of cars, upon any railroad track at the crossing of any traveled street,
or crossing, or alley intersecting such railroad, in the city limits, shall
obstruct the free passageway across the same for a longer time than five (5)
minutes, and any railroad company, its engineers, conductors or other
employees, who shall so obstruct the free passageway along any of such streets,
crossings or alleys for a longer period than above provided shall be subject to
penalty. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-15: LEAVING OBSTRUCTIONS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to place or leave, or cause to be placed or
left, any encroachment, encumbrance or obstruction in or upon any street, alley
or sidewalk, and any person so doing shall be in all cases liable to the city
and to any private person for all damages or injury arising from the same.
(Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-16: PERMISSION TO CONSTRUCT SIDEWALK:
It shall be unlawful for any person to, by himself or agent, lay, build or
place any sidewalk in, upon or along any street without having first obtained
permission therefor from the city council. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-17: STRIPS FOR LAWNS PERMITTED:
For the purpose of improving the looks of the streets and to encourage the
destruction of the weeds thereon, all persons may, in front of their premises
outside the business part of the city, use a strip not more than eight feet
(8') in width outside of the walk along and in front of such premises for a
lawn, and for that purpose may raise such strip by sodding or filling same up
with earth to a level with their lot or lots, under the direction of the street
commissioner and chairperson of the street committee. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-18: UNIFORM WIDTH OF PARKINGS:
The city street commissioner shall require all persons making such improvements
in front of their premises to have a proper regard for the width of the lawns
of the adjoining owners, and, if practicable, to require them to be uniform in
width; such widths to be determined by the chairperson of the street committee.
(Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-19: DRIVING ON PARKINGS:
Any person driving any team, wagon or other vehicle, or riding or driving any
horse, cow, steer, hog or other animals on or across any such lawns, or
wilfully or carelessly permits any such animal to go upon the same, shall be
deemed guilty of a misdemeanor. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-20: DISTURB VEHICLES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to, without the consent of the owner or
driver of any automobile, motor bicycle or horse drawn vehicle, disturb the
same or the contents thereof. (Ord. 11, 2-6-1917)
8-1-21: DATUM PLANE:
The permanent grades of streets and alleys in the city are referred to a plane
as the base, or datum, for all city levels. Said plane referred to is mean sea
level and the elevation of the top of the valve stem of the public fire
hydrants at the intersection of Arch Street and Race Street being 719.84 feet
above datum, is hereby established as a bench mark for the reference of city
elevations. (4-5-1915)
8-1-22: TREES, PLANTING ALONG STREETS:
   (A)   Species And Intervals Of Trees Approved For Planting: The species of
trees, and the intervals between them, approved for planting in the streets of
the city are: ginkgos, thirty feet (30'); ash, Norway maple, Schwendler maple,
red maple, sweet gum, tulip, red oak, white oak, willow oak, scarlet oak,
American linden and European linden, forty feet (40'); pin oak, forty five feet
(45'); honey locust, fifty feet (50').
In addition to the species of trees above permitted, other species of trees may
be approved for planting along the streets of this city as may be specified by
the appropriate committee of the city council.
   (B)   Forbidden Species Of Trees: No person shall plant any of the following
named trees in the streets of the city: evergreens; fruit and nut trees (except
oak); box elder; silver maple; ailanthus; poplar; cottonwood; willow; catalpa;
hackberry; dogwood; white fringe; red bud or elm (including Chinese elm). (Ord.
81-80, 12-1-1981)
8-1-23: PAVED AND/OR ASPHALTED DRIVEWAYS:
Each owner of a lot located within the corporate limits of the city which has a
paved and/or asphalted driveway upon said lot extending past the lot line shall
be required to cut a seam in said driveway parallel with and even with the lot
line. Said seam shall be cut at the expense of the owner of the lot. (Ord. 98-
02, 4-7-1998)
8-1-24: RURAL ROUTE MAILBOXES:
   (A)   Postal Requirements: All mailboxes in the city intended as the
receptacle of the U.S. mail shall meet those requirements of the United States
postal service for the delivery of the U.S. mail.
   (B)   Additional Placement Standards: The city, in addition to the
requirements of the United States postal service, shall require these
additional placement standards:
      1.   On noncurbed streets, the rural mailbox shall be placed a sufficient
distance from the street to allow the mail delivery vehicle to be parked at the
rural mailbox without impairing the flow of traffic on the street.
      2.   On curbed streets, that part of the mailbox closest to the street in
a line perpendicular to the exterior wall of the curbing.
   (C)   Penalty: Violation of subsection (B) of this section shall result in a
twenty five dollar ($25.00) per day fine, or may be enforced by injunctive
relief requiring the removal of the rural mailbox from any placement that
violates this section. (Ord. 03-03, 4-1-2003)
CHAPTER 2
CEMETERY
SECTION:
8-2-1: Cemetery Designated
8-2-2: Conformance Report Required
8-2-3: Supervision
8-2-4: License Required
8-2-5: Violation
8-2-1: CEMETERY DESIGNATED:
The tracts or lots of land purchased by the town, now the city of Atlanta, of
Harvey Turner and Elizabeth Turner, his wife, and particularly described in the
deed from them to the city, recorded in the recorder's office of Logan County,
Illinois, be set apart and dedicated to cemetery purposes and uses, to be kept
and controlled by the corporate authorities of the city.
Said tracts of land, and any other that may hereafter be purchased for cemetery
purposes, or as additions to said grounds, shall be under the control of the
Ladies' Cemetery Association in conformity with the deed from the city to the
association. (Ord. 17, 2-6-1917)
8-2-2: CONFORMANCE REPORT REQUIRED:
The Ladies' Cemetery Association shall at all times conform to the provisions
of this code in regard to the cemetery, as provided in the deed to the
association, and shall make to the city council an annual report of the
condition of said cemetery, which report shall be full and complete in all
particulars regarding said cemetery. (Ord. 17, 2-6-1917)
8-2-3: SUPERVISION:
All work done in the cemetery shall be done under the direction of the board of
directors of the Ladies' Cemetery Association. (Ord. 17, 2-6-1917)
8-2-4: LICENSE REQUIRED:
No person shall do any work of any kind or character in the cemetery without
first having obtained a license therefor; provided, that this shall not apply
to any owner of a lot in said cemetery when working upon his own lot, or to the
members of the immediate family when working upon the lot owned by the family.
The fee for the license provided in this section shall be one dollar ($1.00)
per annum for each lot upon which any work is done by the party holding such
license, payable to the city clerk in advance.
The license fee provided herein shall, when collected by the city clerk, be
turned over to the Ladies' Cemetery Association. (Ord. 17, 2-6-1917)
8-2-5: VIOLATION:
